---
title: "System can't find home partition after upgrade"
date: 2008-04-24
forum: Installation &amp; Upgrades

### Post by Repabil on 2008-04-24
Hello,

Did an upgrade to Hardy on my desktop today. It went successfully until I rebooted into the upgraded system. It fails with ```
ef2fsck: Cannot continue, aborting.

fsck died with exit status 8

File system check failed.
```
Seems my home partition is not mounted. I tried reverting to my old /etc/fstab without success. Is there a way to generate a new /etc/fstab or another way to solve this problem?

---

### Post by dstew on 2008-04-24
Post the output of```
sudo fdisk -l
cat /etc/fstab
```

### Post by dstew on 2008-04-24
Since the problem seems to be with the filesystem check, you can change the line in fstab to```
/dev/sdb1 /home ext3 defaults 0 0
```to turn off the check, and see if it mounts. If it does, you can unmount it, then do the fsck from the command line to see if there are any problems on that partition.

---

### Post by prshah on 2008-04-24
> **Repabil said:**
> Hello,
Did an upgrade to Hardy on my desktop today. It went successfully until I rebooted into the upgraded system. It fails with Seems my home partition is not mounted. I tried reverting to my old /etc/fstab without success. Is there a way to generate a new /etc/fstab or another way to solve this problem?

In your current fstab, replace the UUID for your home partition with the actual partition name, eg. /dev/sda3 or whatever your home partition is.

Eg. change> ```
cat /etc/fstab | grep -i -B 2 home
# /dev/sda7
[color=red]UUID=553b2304-d5e7-4b84-8e2a-4b38ab103cc2[/color] /home           ext3    defaults        0       2

```

to > ```

# /dev/sda7
[color=red]/dev/sda7[/color] /home           ext3    defaults        0       2

```

EDIT: Just saw your /etc/fstab, my post hence becomes irrelevant.

### Post by Holy Cheater on 2008-04-24
[FONT=monospace]Seems like X couldn't find the driver for you video-card. You could change the device section of **/etc/X11/xorg.conf **```
sudo nano /etc/X11/xorg.conf
``` or while booted from liveCD with gedit.

From something like this:
```

Section "Device"
        Identifier      "GeForce 8800GT"
        Boardname       "Palit GeForce 8800GT Super + 1GB"
        Busid           "PCI:1:0:0"
        Driver          "nvidia"
        Option          "NoLogo" "true"
        Option          "DPI" "96 x 96"
        Screen  0
EndSection

```to something like this:
```

Section "Device"
        Identifier      "GeForce 8800GT"
        Boardname       "Palit GeForce 8800GT Super + 1GB"
        Busid           "PCI:1:0:0"
**        Driver          "vesa"**
        Screen  0
EndSection

```Still, it won't fully fix the problem.

Have you tried to recompile nvidia driver from **NVIDIA-*pkg1.run**?
[/FONT]

---

### Post by Peter09 on 2008-04-24
your sudo problem is to do with your host name in /etc/hostname.

Go to recovery mode and change your hostname to a single word in /etc/hostname.

PC

---

### Post by Holy Cheater on 2008-04-24
Don't know if it will help, but try this: (changes in bold)
```

# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by failsafeDexconf, using
# values from the debconf database and some overrides to use vesa mode.
#
# You should use dexconf or another such tool for creating a "real" xorg.conf
# For example:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg
Section "InputDevice"
    Identifier    "Generic Keyboard"
    Driver        "kbd"
    **Option        "CoreKeyboard"**
    Option        "XkbRules"    "xorg"
    Option        "XkbModel"    "pc105"
    Option        "XkbLayout"    "se"
    Option        "XkbVariant"    "se"

    Identifier    "Configured Mouse"
    Driver        "mouse"

    Boardname    "vesa"
    Busid        "PCI:3:0:0"
    Driver        "vesa"
    Screen    0

About the hostname:
You should check **/etc/hostname** file, not **/etc/hosts**

---

### Post by Repabil on 2008-04-25
Thanks for the help everyone.

[LIST]
[*]Correct my /etc/fstab. Hardy kernel or something seems to have changed up the names in /dev so I had to get em right in /etc/fstab by looking at fdisk -l.
[*]Add 'Option "CoreKeyboard"' to keyboard bit in xorg.conf to be able to use keyboard in X
[*]Get video and screen bits from my old x.org to have the right settings in hardy X
[/LIST]

Got around the sudo problem by mounting drives from live-CD.

---
